<p><a href="/wiki/Pan_European_Game_Information" title="Pan European Game Information">Pan European Game Information</a> (PEGI) is a system that was developed to standardize the game ratings in all of Europe (not just <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, although the majority are EU members), the current members are: all EU members, except Germany and the 10 accession states; <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>; <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>. Iceland is expected to join soon, as are the 10 EU accession states. For all PEGI members, they use it as their sole system, with the exception of the UK, where if a game contains certain material,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> it must be rated by <a href="/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification" title="British Board of Film Classification">BBFC</a>. The PEGI ratings are legally binding in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and it is a criminal offence to sell a game to someone if it is rated above their age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany:_BPjM_and_USK">Germany: BPjM and USK</span></h3>
<p>Stricter game rating laws mean that Germany does not operate within the PEGI. Instead, they adopt their own system of certification which is required by law. The <a href="/wiki/Unterhaltungssoftware_Selbstkontrolle" title="Unterhaltungssoftware Selbstkontrolle">Unterhaltungssoftware Selbstkontrolle</a> (<i>USK</i> or Voluntary Certification of Entertainment Software) checks every game before release and assigns an age rating to it â€“ either none (white), 6 years of age (yellow), 12 years of age (green), 16 years of age (blue) or 18 years of age (red). It is forbidden for anyone, retailers, friends or parents alike, to allow a child access to a game for which he or she is underage. If a game is considered to be harmful to young people (for example because of extremely violent, pornographic or racist content), it may be referred to the BPjM (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bundespr%C3%BCfstelle_f%C3%BCr_jugendgef%C3%A4hrdende_Medien" title="BundesprÃ¼fstelle fÃ¼r jugendgefÃ¤hrdende Medien">BundesprÃ¼fstelle fÃ¼r jugendgefÃ¤hrdende Medien</a></i> â€“ Federal Verification Office for Child-Endangering Media) who may opt to place it on the Index upon which the game may not be sold openly or advertised in the open media. Such indexed titles are not "banned" and can still be legally obtained by adults, but it is considered a felony to supply these titles to a child.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_aspects">Commercial aspects</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_sales">Game sales</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">Video game industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_video_games" title="List of best-selling video games">List of best-selling video games</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_arcade_video_games" title="Golden age of arcade video games">Golden age of arcade video games</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Videogameretaildisplay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Videogameretaildisplay.jpg/220px-Videogameretaildisplay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Videogameretaildisplay.jpg/330px-Videogameretaildisplay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Videogameretaildisplay.jpg/440px-Videogameretaildisplay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Videogameretaildisplay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A retail display with a large selection of games for platforms popular in the early 2000s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the market research firm SuperData, as of May 2015, the global games market was worth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">USD</a> 74.2 billion. By region, North America accounted for $23.6 billion, Asia for $23.1 billion, Europe for $22.1 billion and South America for $4.5 billion. By market segment, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile games</a> were worth $22.3 billion, retail games 19.7 billion, <a href="/wiki/Free-to-play" title="Free-to-play">free-to-play</a> <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_game" title="Massively multiplayer online game">MMOs</a> 8.7 billion, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_games" title="Social games">social games</a> $7.9 billion, PC <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">DLC</a> 7.5 billion, and other categories $3 billion or less each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SuperData_2015_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-SuperData_2015-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, also according to SuperData, the share of video games in the entertainment market grew from 5% in 1985 to 13% in 2015, becoming the third-largest market segment behind broadcast and cable television. The research firm anticipated that Asia would soon overtake North America as the largest video game market due to the strong growth of free-to-play and mobile games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SuperData_2015_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-SuperData_2015-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sales of different types of games vary widely between countries due to local preferences. Japanese consumers tend to purchase much more <a href="/wiki/Console_game" title="Console game">console games</a> than <a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">computer games</a>, with a strong preference for games catering to local tastes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Another key difference is that, despite the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_video_arcade_games" title="Golden age of video arcade games">decline of arcades in the West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcade_game" title="Arcade game">arcade games</a> remain the largest sector of the <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Japan" title="Video gaming in Japan">Japanese gaming industry</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_South_Korea" title="Video gaming in South Korea">In South Korea</a>, computer games are generally preferred over console games, especially <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_role-playing_game" title="Massively multiplayer online role-playing game">MMORPG</a> games and <a href="/wiki/Real-time_strategy" title="Real-time strategy">real-time strategy</a> games. Computer games are also popular in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conventions">Conventions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_gaming_conventions" title="List of gaming conventions">List of gaming conventions</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_(5473).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2300" data-file-width="3300" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg/220px-Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg/330px-Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg/440px-Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_%285473%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gamescom_2009_-_Koelnmesse_S%C3%BCdeingang_(5473).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Gamescom" title="Gamescom">gamescom</a> fair in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gaming_convention" title="Gaming convention">Gaming conventions</a> are an important showcase of the industry. The annual <a href="/wiki/Gamescom" title="Gamescom">gamescom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> in August is the world's leading expo for video games in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamescom1_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamescom1-88">[88]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3</a> in June in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> is also of global importance, but is an event for industry insiders only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Game_Show" title="Tokyo Game Show">Tokyo Game Show</a> in September is the main fair in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.</p>
<p>Other notable conventions and trade fairs include <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Game_Show" title="Brasil Game Show">Brasil Game Show</a> in October, <a href="/wiki/Paris_Games_Week" title="Paris Games Week">Paris Games Week</a> in Octoberâ€“November, <a href="/wiki/EB_Games_Expo" title="EB Games Expo">EB Games Expo</a> (Australia) in October, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Game_Developers_Conference" title="Russian Game Developers Conference">KRI</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Digital_Entertainment_Expo_%26_Conference" title="China Digital Entertainment Expo &amp; Conference">ChinaJoy</a> in July and the annual <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">Game Developers Conference</a>.</p>
<p>Some publishers, developers and technology producers also host their own regular conventions, with <a href="/wiki/BlizzCon" title="BlizzCon">BlizzCon</a>, <a href="/wiki/QuakeCon" title="QuakeCon">QuakeCon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nvision" title="Nvision">Nvision</a> and the <a href="/wiki/X_(Xbox_show)" title="X (Xbox show)">X shows</a> being prominent examples.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="eSports">eSports</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ESports" title="ESports">eSports</a></div>
<p>Short for electronic sports, are video game competitions played most by professional players individually or in teams that gained pupularity from late 2000s, the most common genres are <a href="/wiki/Fighting_game" title="Fighting game">fighting</a>, <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a> (FPS), <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer_online_battle_arena" title="Multiplayer online battle arena">multiplayer online battle arena</a> (MOBA) and <a href="/wiki/Real-time_strategy" title="Real-time strategy">real-time strategy</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg/220px-Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg/330px-Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg/440px-Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Consoles-computerspielemuseum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gaming consoles at the <a href="/wiki/Computerspielemuseum_Berlin" title="Computerspielemuseum Berlin">Computer Games Museum</a> in Berlin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are many video game museums around the world, including the <a href="/wiki/Computerspielemuseum_Berlin" title="Computerspielemuseum Berlin">Computer Games Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Soviet_Arcade_Machines" title="Museum of Soviet Arcade Machines">Museum of Soviet Arcade Machines</a> in Moscow and Saint-Petersburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Art_and_Digital_Entertainment" title="Museum of Art and Digital Entertainment">Museum of Art and Digital Entertainment</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a> is a dedicated video game museum focusing on playable exhibits of console and computer games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Video_Game_Museum_of_Rome" title="Video Game Museum of Rome">Video Game Museum of Rome</a> is also dedicated to preserving video games and their history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Center_for_the_History_of_Electronic_Games" title="International Center for the History of Electronic Games">International Center for the History of Electronic Games</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Strong" title="The Strong">The Strong</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a> contains one of the largest collections of electronic games and game-related historical materials in the world, including a 5,000-square-foot (460Â m<sup>2</sup>) exhibit which allows guests to play their way through the history of video games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a> in Washington, D.C. has three video games on permanent display: <i>Pac-Man</i>, <i>Dragon's Lair</i>, and <i>Pong</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">Museum of Modern Art</a> has added a total of <a href="/wiki/List_of_video_games_in_the_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="List of video games in the Museum of Modern Art">20 video games and one video game console</a> to its permanent Architecture and Design Collection since 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_American_Art_Museum" title="Smithsonian American Art Museum">Smithsonian American Art Museum</a> ran an exhibition on "<a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Video_Games" title="The Art of Video Games">The Art of Video Games</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> However, the reviews of the exhibit were mixed, including questioning whether video games belong in an art museum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
